<span id="page-66-1"></span>In this section, we show how to obtain a witness encryption scheme from any 2-message predictable argument. Our construction largely follows the corresponding construction of Faonio et al. [FNV17], except we additionally consider schemes with imperfect completeness.

{67}------------------------------------------------

Construction E.1 (Witness Encryption from Predictable Argument [FNV17, adapted]). Let  $\Pi_{LA} = (\mathcal{Q}_{LA}, \mathcal{V}_{LA})$  be a predictable 2-message laconic argument for an NP relation  $\mathcal{R}$ . Suppose the prover's message can be expressed as an  $\ell$ -bit string (i.e., elements of  $\{0,1\}^{\ell}$ ). We construct a witness encryption scheme  $\Pi_{WE} = (\text{Encrypt}, \text{Decrypt})$  for  $\mathcal{R}$  as follows:

- Encrypt( $1^{\lambda}$ , x, m) On input the security parameter  $\lambda$ , a statement x and a message bit  $m \in \{0, 1\}$ , the encryption algorithm samples a random  $r \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}^{\ell}$  and runs  $(q, \mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^{\lambda}, x)$ , where  $\mathsf{st} \in \{0, 1\}^{\ell}$ . Compute  $\mathsf{ct} = (q, r, m \oplus \langle r, \mathsf{st} \rangle)$ . Here, we write  $\langle r, \mathsf{st} \rangle$  to denote the inner product between  $r, \mathsf{st} \in \{0, 1\}^{\ell}$  (viewed as vectors in  $\mathbb{F}_2^{\ell}$ ).
- Decrypt $(w, \mathsf{ct})$ : On input a ciphertext  $\mathsf{ct} = (q, r, m')$  and a witness w, the decryption algorithm computes  $\pi \leftarrow \mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{LA}}(q, x, w) \in \{0, 1\}^{\ell}$  and outputs  $\langle r, \pi \rangle \oplus m'$ .

**Theorem E.2** (Witness Encryption from Predictable Arguments). If  $\Pi_{\mathsf{LA}}$  is a predictable 2-message argument for  $\mathcal{R}$  with completeness error c and soundness error  $\varepsilon = \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , then  $\Pi_{\mathsf{WE}}$  from Construction E.1 is a witness encryption scheme for  $\mathcal{R}$  with correctness error c/2.

*Proof.* We show correctness and semantic security.

- Correctness: Take any  $(x, w) \in \mathcal{R}$  and  $m \in \{0, 1\}$ . Let  $\mathsf{ct} = (q, r, m') \leftarrow \mathsf{Encrypt}(1^\lambda, x, m)$ . In this case,  $(q, \mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^\lambda, x), \ r \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}^\ell$ , and  $m' = m \oplus \langle r, \mathsf{st} \rangle$ . Consider  $\mathsf{Decrypt}(\mathsf{ct}, w)$ . The decryption algorithm  $\mathsf{Decrypt}(w, \mathsf{ct})$  begins by computing  $\pi \leftarrow \mathcal{P}_{\mathsf{LA}}(q, x, w)$ . We consider two possibilities:
  - By completeness of  $\Pi_{LA}$ , with probability 1-c,  $\pi=st$  (since  $\Pi_{LA}$  is predictable). In this case, the decryption algorithm correctly outputs m.
  - With probability  $c, \pi \neq \mathsf{st}$ . Moreover, in this case, the value of  $\pi$  is computed independently of r (namely,  $\pi$  depends only on q, x, w while r was sampled uniformly at random from  $\{0, 1\}^{\ell}$ ). By pairwise independence, if  $\pi \neq \mathsf{st}$ ,

$$\Pr[\langle r, \pi \rangle = \langle r, \mathsf{st} \rangle \mid r \overset{\mathtt{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}^{\ell}] = 1/2.$$

Thus, the decryption algorithm outputs m with probability 1/2 in this case.

Thus, we see that

$$\Pr[\mathsf{Decrypt}(w,\mathsf{ct}) = m \mid \mathsf{ct} \leftarrow \mathsf{Encrypt}(1^\lambda,x,m)] = 1 - c + \frac{c}{2} = 1 - \frac{c}{2}.$$

<span id="page-67-0"></span>• Semantic security: Our analysis will rely on the classic Goldreich-Levin theorem [GL89], a version of which we state below:

**Theorem E.3** (Goldreich-Levin). Take any  $\varepsilon > 0$ . Fix some  $x \in \{0,1\}^n$  and let  $\mathcal{A}_x$  be an efficient (and possibly randomized) algorithm where  $\Pr[\mathcal{A}_x(r) = \langle r, x \rangle \mid r \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^n] \geq 1/2 + \varepsilon$ . There exists a poly $(n, 1/\varepsilon)$ -time decoding algorithm  $\mathcal{D}^{\mathcal{A}_x(\cdot)}$  that given oracle access to  $\mathcal{A}_x$ , outputs a list  $L \subseteq \{0,1\}^n$  such that  $|L| = \mathsf{poly}(n, 1/\varepsilon)$  and  $x \in L$  with probability at least 1/2.

Turning back to semantic security, suppose that there exists an efficient adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  and some  $x \notin \mathcal{L}$  such that

$$\Pr[\mathcal{A}(1^{\lambda},\mathsf{ct}_b) = b \mid b \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}, \mathsf{ct}_b \leftarrow \mathsf{Encrypt}(1^{\lambda},x,b)] \geq \frac{1}{2} + \varepsilon.$$

for some  $\varepsilon = 1/\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ . Let t be a bound on the number of bits of randomness needed by  $\mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}$ . Namely, to sample  $(q,\mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^{\lambda},x)$ , one first samples  $\rho \stackrel{\mathsf{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^t$  and then computes  $(q,\mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^{\lambda},x;\rho)$ . This means that

$$\Pr\left[\mathcal{A}(1^{\lambda}, (q, r, b \oplus \langle r, \mathsf{st} \rangle)) = b \;\middle|\;\; \begin{array}{c} b \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}, r \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}^{\ell}, \rho \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}^{t}; \\ (q, \mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^{\lambda}, x; \rho) \end{array}\right] \geq \frac{1}{2} + \varepsilon.$$

We use  $\mathcal{A}$  to construct an algorithm  $\mathcal{B}$  that on input (q,r) predicts the value of  $\langle r, \mathsf{st} \rangle$ , where  $(q, \mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^{\lambda}, x)$  and  $r \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}^{\ell}$ :

{68}------------------------------------------------

- On input (q, r), algorithm  $\mathcal{B}$  samples  $b \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}$  and invokes  $\mathcal{A}$  on input (q, r, b). If  $\mathcal{A}$  outputs b, then  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs 0. Otherwise  $\mathcal{B}$  outputs 1.

It is easy to see that by construction,

$$\Pr\left[\mathcal{B}(1^{\lambda},(q,r)) = \langle r,\mathsf{st}\rangle \;\middle|\; \begin{array}{c} r \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{\ell}, \rho \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^{t}; \\ (q,\mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^{\lambda},x;\rho) \end{array}\right] \geq \frac{1}{2} + \varepsilon.$$

We use  $\mathcal{B}$  to construct an adversary  $\mathcal{B}'$  that breaks soundness of  $\Pi_{\mathsf{LA}}$  (for the instance  $x \notin \mathcal{L}$ ):

- 1. On input the security parameter  $\lambda$ , the instance x, and the query q, run the Goldreich-Levin list-decoding algorithm  $\mathcal{D}^{\mathcal{B}(1^{\lambda},(q,\cdot))}$  (Theorem E.3) where the oracle queries are implemented as follows:
  - On input  $r \in \{0,1\}^{\ell}$ , output  $\mathcal{B}(1^{\lambda},(q,r))$ .

Let  $L \subseteq \{0,1\}^{\ell}$  be the list output by the list-decoding algorithm.

2. Output  $\pi \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} L$ .

We now analyze the success probability of algorithm  $\mathcal{B}'$ . First, for a fixed element  $\rho \in \{0,1\}^t$  and the associated query  $(q, \mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^\lambda, x; \rho)$ , define the algorithm  $\mathcal{B}_\rho(r)$  to be the algorithm that on input  $r \in \{0,1\}^\ell$  outputs  $\mathcal{B}(1^\lambda, (q,r))$ . Let  $S \subseteq \{0,1\}^t$  be the set of elements  $\rho \in \{0,1\}^t$  such that

<span id="page-68-0"></span>
$$\Pr[\mathcal{B}_{\rho}(r) = \langle r, \mathsf{st} \rangle \mid r \overset{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0, 1\}^{\ell}, (q, \mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^{\lambda}, x; \rho)] \ge \frac{1}{2} + \frac{\varepsilon}{2}. \tag{E.1}$$

By an averaging argument,

$$\Pr[\rho \in S \mid \rho \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^t] \ge \varepsilon.$$

In the soundness game, the challenger begins by sampling  $\rho \stackrel{\mathbb{R}}{\leftarrow} \{0,1\}^t$  and  $(q, \mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^\lambda, x; \rho)$ , and algorithm  $\mathcal{B}'$  is given as input  $(1^\lambda, x, q)$ . Thus, with probability  $\varepsilon$ , the randomness  $\rho$  sampled by the challenger lies in the set S. In this case, the oracle  $\mathcal{B}(1^\lambda, (q, \cdot)) \equiv \mathcal{B}_{\rho}(\cdot)$  in  $\mathcal{B}'$  satisfies Eq. (E.1), so we can appeal to the Goldreich-Levin theorem (Theorem E.3) to conclude that the list L output by  $\mathcal{D}^{\mathcal{B}(1^\lambda, (q, \cdot))}$  contains st with probability at least 1/2. If  $\mathsf{st} \in L$ , then  $\mathcal{B}'$  outputs  $\mathsf{st}$  with probability 1/|L|, and since  $\Pi_{\mathsf{LA}}$  is predictable,  $\mathcal{V}_{\mathsf{LA}}(\mathsf{st}, \mathsf{st}) = 1$ . Thus,  $\mathcal{B}'$  breaks soundness with probability

$$\Pr[\mathcal{B}'(1^{\lambda}, x, q) = \mathsf{st} \mid (q, \mathsf{st}) \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{\mathsf{LA}}(1^{\lambda}, x)] \geq \varepsilon \cdot \frac{1}{2} \cdot \frac{1}{|L|} = \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\ell, 1/\varepsilon)} = \frac{1}{\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)},$$

since  $\ell = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  and  $\varepsilon = 1/\mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$  by assumption. Moreover, the running time of  $\mathcal{B}'$  is bounded by the product of the running times of the list-decoding algorithm and the running time of  $\mathcal{B}$ , both of which are  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda,\ell,1/\varepsilon) = \mathsf{poly}(\lambda)$ . Thus,  $\mathcal{B}'$  breaks soundness with non-negligible probability and the claim holds.
